- **Source**: [external/src/index.ts:147](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/external/src/index.ts#L147), [external/src/index.ts:193](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/external/src/index.ts#L193), [memory-crud-delete.ts:67](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-crud-delete.ts#L67), [memory-crud-update.ts:138](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-crud-update.ts#L138); evidence: both
- **What it does**: Mnemosyne exposes append-plus-delete behavior at the wrapper boundary, while Public wraps updates/deletes in transactions, history, ledgering, checkpointing, and hook invalidation.
- **Why it matters for us**: Public should keep its auditable mutation model and treat contradiction cleanup as structured revision, not as plain-text ID deletion.

### Finding 9: A native OpenCode memory plugin is viable only as a delegation-only facade
- **Source**: [external/package.json:31](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/external/package.json#L31), [external/src/index.ts:38](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/external/src/index.ts#L38), [session-bootstrap.ts:330](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/session-bootstrap.ts#L330), [opencode-transport.ts:104](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/lib/context/opencode-transport.ts#L104); evidence: both

- **Source**: [external/README.md:18](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/external/README.md#L18), [external/src/index.ts:67](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/external/src/index.ts#L67), [context-server.ts:751](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/context-server.ts#L751), [session-bootstrap.ts:194](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/session-bootstrap.ts#L194); evidence: both

40:Research Mex's markdown scaffold and drift detection patterns to identify practical, evidence-backed improvements for `Code_Environment/Public`, especially around staleness detection, codebase-knowledge synchronization, and structured project knowledge. Determine which Mex patterns should be `adopt now`, `prototype later`, or `reject`.
46:Mex is a structured markdown scaffold with a TypeScript/Node.js CLI for persistent AI project memory. Instead of a database, it keeps project knowledge in navigable markdown files such as `AGENTS.md`, `ROUTER.md`, `context/*.md`, and `patterns/*.md`. Its defining mechanism is drift detection: eight static checkers validate scaffold claims against the real codebase without AI or token spend. Those checkers cover path validation, frontmatter edges, pattern index consistency, staleness based on git history, command existence, dependency claims, cross-file contradictions, and script coverage. Drift starts at score `100` and deducts `-10` per error, `-3` per warning, and `-1` per info. The scaffold is designed to grow after real work through pattern creation, targeted context updates, and current-state refreshes rather than one-time setup alone.
59:`Code_Environment/Public` already has Spec Kit validation via `validate.sh` with severity-oriented checks, indexed memory files with frontmatter, and a `MEMORY.md`-style documentation/memory model. What it does **not** currently have is an automated drift checker that compares documentation or memory scaffolds against the actual filesystem, commands, dependencies, git staleness, or cross-file contradictions. Research should stay centered on that gap rather than re-covering general memory persistence already addressed by phase `001`.
72:10. Examine the next three drift checkers individually: `src/drift/checkers/staleness.ts`, `src/drift/checkers/command.ts`, and `src/drift/checkers/dependency.ts`. Capture the exact thresholds and matching rules, including how staleness uses both days and commit counts, how commands are validated, and how dependency claims are compared to manifests.

// ╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
// ║ Spec Kit Compact Code Graph OpenCode Plugin                              ║
// ╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝
'use strict';

// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// 1. OVERVIEW
// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// Thin OpenCode plugin hook layer for packet 030.
// Important runtime boundary: never import the MCP server bundle directly
// inside the OpenCode host process because its native modules (better-sqlite3,
// sqlite-vec) may be compiled for a different Node ABI than the host runtime.
// Instead, call a plain `node` bridge process that loads the server bundle in
// the user's normal Node environment and returns the transport plan as JSON.

// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// 2. IMPORTS
// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

import { randomUUID } from 'node:crypto';
import { execFile } from 'node:child_process';
import { fileURLToPath } from 'node:url';

import { tool } from '@opencode-ai/plugin';
import {
  createSyntheticTextPart,
  hasUnsafeMessageTransformParts,
  hasSyntheticTextPartMarker,
  isMessageAnchorLike,
} from './spec-kit-opencode-message-schema.mjs';

// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// 3. CONSTANTS AND TYPES
// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

const PLUGIN_ID = 'spec-kit-compact-code-graph';
const DEFAULT_CACHE_TTL_MS = 5000;
const DEFAULT_BRIDGE_TIMEOUT_MS = 15000;
const DEFAULT_NODE_BINARY = 'node';
const RESUME_MODE = 'minimal';
const MESSAGES_TRANSFORM_ENABLED = true;
const MESSAGES_TRANSFORM_MODE = 'schema_aligned';
const SYNTHETIC_METADATA_KEY = 'specKitCompactCodeGraph';
const BRIDGE_PATH = fileURLToPath(new URL('./spec-kit-compact-code-graph-bridge.mjs', import.meta.url));

/**
 * @typedef {{
 *   cacheTtlMs?: number,
 *   specFolder?: string,
 *   nodeBinary?: string,
 *   bridgeTimeoutMs?: number,
 * }} PluginOptions
 */

/**
 * @typedef {{
 *   hook: string,
 *   title: string,
 *   payloadKind: string,
 *   dedupeKey: string,
 *   content: string,
 * }} TransportBlock
 */

/**
 * @typedef {{
 *   interfaceVersion: string,
 *   transportOnly: true,
 *   retrievalPolicyOwner: string,
 *   event: {
 *     hook: string,
 *     trackedPayloadKinds: string[],
 *     summary: string,
 *   },
 *   systemTransform?: TransportBlock,
 *   messagesTransform: TransportBlock[],
 *   compaction?: TransportBlock,
 * }} TransportPlan
 */

// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// 4. MODULE STATE
// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

const transportCache = new Map();
let runtimeReady = false;
let lastRuntimeError = null;

// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// 5. HELPERS
// ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

function normalizePositiveInt(value, fallback) {
  return Number.isFinite(value) && value > 0 ? Math.trunc(value) : fallback;
}

function normalizeOptions(rawOptions) {
  if (!rawOptions || typeof rawOptions !== 'object') {
    return {
      cacheTtlMs: DEFAULT_CACHE_TTL_MS,
      specFolder: undefined,
      nodeBinary: process.env.SPEC_KIT_PLUGIN_NODE_BINARY || DEFAULT_NODE_BINARY,
      bridgeTimeoutMs: DEFAULT_BRIDGE_TIMEOUT_MS,
    };
  }

  const options = /** @type {PluginOptions} */ (rawOptions);
  return {
    cacheTtlMs: normalizePositiveInt(options.cacheTtlMs, DEFAULT_CACHE_TTL_MS),
    specFolder: typeof options.specFolder === 'string' && options.specFolder.trim()
      ? options.specFolder.trim()
      : undefined,
    nodeBinary: typeof options.nodeBinary === 'string' && options.nodeBinary.trim()
      ? options.nodeBinary.trim()
      : (process.env.SPEC_KIT_PLUGIN_NODE_BINARY || DEFAULT_NODE_BINARY),
    bridgeTimeoutMs: normalizePositiveInt(options.bridgeTimeoutMs, DEFAULT_BRIDGE_TIMEOUT_MS),
  };
}

function cacheKeyForSession(sessionID, specFolder) {
  return `${specFolder ?? '__workspace__'}::${sessionID ?? '__global__'}`;
}

function parseTransportPlan(responseText) {
  if (!responseText) {
    return null;
  }

  try {
    const parsed = JSON.parse(responseText);
    const data = parsed?.data ?? parsed;
    const plan = data?.opencodeTransport;
    if (!plan || typeof plan !== 'object') {
      return null;
    }
    if (plan.transportOnly !== true || !Array.isArray(plan.messagesTransform)) {
      return null;
    }
    return /** @type {TransportPlan} */ (plan);
  } catch {
    return null;
  }
}

function stringifyError(error) {
  if (!error) {
    return 'Unknown bridge error';
  }
  if (error instanceof Error) {
    return error.message;
  }
  return String(error);
}

function execFilePromise(file, args, options) {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    execFile(file, args, options, (error, stdout, stderr) => {
      if (error) {
        reject(error);
        return;
      }
      resolve({
        stdout: typeof stdout === 'string' ? stdout : '',
        stderr: typeof stderr === 'string' ? stderr : '',
      });
    });
  });
}

async function runTransportBridge({ projectDir, specFolder, nodeBinary, bridgeTimeoutMs }) {
  const args = [BRIDGE_PATH, '--minimal'];
  if (specFolder) {
    args.push('--spec-folder', specFolder);
  }

  const result = await execFilePromise(nodeBinary, args, {
    cwd: projectDir,
    env: process.env,
    timeout: bridgeTimeoutMs,
    maxBuffer: 1024 * 1024,
  });
  return parseTransportPlan(result.stdout.trim());
}

async function loadTransportPlan({ projectDir, sessionID, specFolder, cacheTtlMs, nodeBinary, bridgeTimeoutMs }) {
  const key = cacheKeyForSession(sessionID, specFolder);
  const now = Date.now();
  const cached = transportCache.get(key);

  if (cached && cached.expiresAt > now) {
    return cached.plan;
  }

  try {
    const plan = await runTransportBridge({
      projectDir,
      specFolder,
      nodeBinary,
      bridgeTimeoutMs,
    });

    if (!plan) {
      lastRuntimeError = 'Bridge returned no OpenCode transport payload';
      runtimeReady = false;
      transportCache.delete(key);
      return null;
    }

    runtimeReady = true;
    lastRuntimeError = null;
    transportCache.set(key, {
      plan,
      expiresAt: now + cacheTtlMs,
      updatedAt: new Date(now).toISOString(),
    });
    return plan;
  } catch (error) {
    runtimeReady = false;
    lastRuntimeError = stringifyError(error);
    transportCache.delete(key);

exec

## Findings
### Finding 1: Static markdown reference integrity is the only clear adopt-now slice
- **Source**: [README.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/README.md#L72), [claims.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/claims.ts#L48), [drift/index.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/index.ts#L17), [path.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/path.ts#L8), [edges.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/edges.ts#L5), [index-sync.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/index-sync.ts#L6)
- **What it does**: Mex extracts typed markdown claims from inline code, code blocks, and dependency headings, then runs zero-token checks for missing paths, dead frontmatter edges, and `patterns/INDEX.md` drift. It already distinguishes real missing references from pattern/template placeholders by downgrading some path misses to warnings.
- **Why it matters for us**: This cleanly maps to our real gap. Spec Kit already has semantic retrieval, trigger recall, causal links, and health tooling, but it does not statically verify that markdown references still point to real files or that pattern indexes stay in sync.
- **Recommendation**: adopt now
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 2: Dual freshness signals are useful, but only as supplemental trust metadata
- **Source**: [staleness.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/staleness.ts#L4), [git.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/git.ts#L12), [shared-payload.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/lib/context/shared-payload.ts#L22), [session-bootstrap.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/session-bootstrap.ts#L219), [memory-triggers.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-triggers.ts#L329)
- **What it does**: Mex emits separate stale-file issues from both elapsed days (`30`/`90`) and commits since last change (`50`/`200`). If git history cannot answer, `git.ts` returns `null`, so the checker silently emits nothing.
- **Why it matters for us**: The days-plus-commits idea is strong, but silent `null` is too weak for Spec Kit. Our current surfaces already distinguish `exact`, `estimated`, `defaulted`, `unknown`, and degraded matching; freshness should plug into that trust model instead of pretending “no signal” means “healthy.”
- **Recommendation**: prototype later
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 3: Mex’s repair brief flow is worth building as a provider-neutral Spec Kit feature
- **Source**: [sync/index.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/sync/index.ts#L29), [brief-builder.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/sync/brief-builder.ts#L7)
- **What it does**: `mex sync` groups issues by file, builds one combined brief, includes the current markdown, issue list, nearby filesystem listings for missing paths, and `HEAD~5..HEAD` diffs for referenced paths, then runs an interactive repair loop and re-checks drift after each cycle.
- **Why it matters for us**: This is the best “AI-assisted” idea in Mex. It converts static failures into bounded, auditable repair work instead of re-running broad doc rewrites. That fits Spec Kit’s packet-local remediation style very well.
- **Recommendation**: NEW FEATURE
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 4: Command, dependency, cross-file, and script-coverage audits are good ideas, but Mex’s implementation is too Node-centric for direct adoption
- **Source**: [command.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/command.ts#L5), [dependency.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/dependency.ts#L38), [cross-file.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/cross-file.ts#L3), [script-coverage.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/script-coverage.ts#L26), [manifest.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/scanner/manifest.ts#L48)
- **What it does**: Mex validates npm/bun/yarn/pnpm scripts and Make targets, checks package dependencies and versions against `package.json`, flags version contradictions across docs, and warns if package scripts never appear in scaffold text. Non-Node manifests are mostly stubbed.
- **Why it matters for us**: We do need broader wrapper/config/doc parity checks, but our truth surfaces span shell commands, MCP tools, Python, TS, generated docs, and spec packets. Mex’s current inventory model is too narrow to trust in our repo.
- **Recommendation**: NEW FEATURE
- **Impact**: medium

### Finding 5: Scanner-first setup briefs are useful for bootstrapping, but not for durable truth maintenance
- **Source**: [README.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/README.md#L50), [SETUP.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/SETUP.md#L13), [scanner/index.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/scanner/index.ts#L20), [manifest.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/scanner/manifest.ts#L12)
- **What it does**: `mex init` builds a structured brief from manifest, entry points, folder tree, tooling, and README, then tells the AI to populate scaffold files from that brief rather than from raw browsing.
- **Why it matters for us**: This is good for first-pass scaffold seeding or packet bootstrap because it reduces exploratory noise. It is not good enough to become an authority layer for Spec Kit memory or documentation parity, especially with shallow non-Node support and no richer trust contract.
- **Recommendation**: prototype later
- **Impact**: low

### Finding 6: Mex’s GROW loop and `pattern add` workflow should not become part of Spec Kit’s default documentation lifecycle
- **Source**: [ROUTER.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/ROUTER.md#L56), [README.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/README.md#L178), [pattern/index.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/pattern/index.ts#L6)
- **What it does**: The contract requires post-task scaffold growth, and `pattern add` immediately creates a task-pattern template plus a placeholder `[description]` row in `patterns/INDEX.md`.
- **Why it matters for us**: In Spec Kit, partially formed docs become durable retrieval material quickly. Mex’s loop optimizes for compounding coverage, but it does so before truth is secured. That is the wrong default for a trust-sensitive memory system.
- **Recommendation**: reject
- **Impact**: medium

### Finding 7: Mex’s single drift score should not be promoted into Spec Kit’s primary health surface
- **Source**: [README.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/README.md#L87), [scoring.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/scoring.ts#L3), [post-save-review.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/scripts/core/post-save-review.ts#L1019), [validate-memory-quality.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/scripts/lib/validate-memory-quality.ts#L45), [shared-payload.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/lib/context/shared-payload.ts#L22)
- **What it does**: Mex starts at `100` and subtracts fixed costs per issue. That makes score the headline surface even though the underlying findings have very different trust implications.
- **Why it matters for us**: Spec Kit already has richer truth states: block-on-write rules, `REJECTED` post-save outcomes, and certainty/provenance fields. A single score would compress those distinctions and make unsafe or unknown states look deceptively acceptable.
- **Recommendation**: reject
- **Impact**: medium

## Assessment
- New information ratio: 0.46
- Questions addressed: markdown-first scaffold tradeoffs; checker composition and blind spots; freshness thresholds and git failure semantics; claim extraction behavior; targeted sync design; post-task scaffold growth; overlap with current Spec Kit validation and trust surfaces
- Questions answered: adopt only static reference integrity now; prototype freshness only with explicit trust semantics; build repair briefs as a new feature; defer inventory-backed parity until a cross-surface model exists; reject auto-growth defaults and reject score-first health

## Reflection
- What worked: tracing Mex in execution order, then comparing each mechanism to current Spec Kit trust and health contracts, made the keep/defer/reject boundaries much clearer than the README alone.
- What did not work: the semantic code search path did not produce usable output in this run, so the synthesis stayed grounded in direct source reads. The validator also emitted the expected sandbox warning about temp-file creation, although it still finished `PASSED`.

## Recommended Next Focus
1. Implement a narrow markdown drift pass for Spec Kit that checks packet-local paths, frontmatter edges, and index/list coherence with severity-first reporting only.
2. Design a freshness prototype that reports `exact` versus `unknown/degraded` authority instead of silently passing when git data is unavailable.
3. Spec a provider-neutral repair-brief tool that converts failed validations into packet-local remediation prompts with file context and recent diffs.
4. Delay broader command/dependency/script parity until there is a shared inventory model across npm, shell, Python, MCP, wrappers, and spec docs.

# Iteration 020: FINAL SYNTHESIS

## Focus
FINAL SYNTHESIS: Classify every major Mex mechanism as `adopt now`, `prototype later`, `NEW FEATURE`, or `reject`.

Executive summary: Mex is strongest as a thin markdown-integrity layer, not as a replacement for Spec Kit Memory. The clear win is narrow static reference integrity for markdown surfaces. Freshness is worth prototyping only if we preserve Spec Kit’s explicit `exact` / `estimated` / `unknown` / blocked semantics. Targeted repair briefs are worth building as a new feature. Inventory-heavy parity checks need a broader abstraction first. Auto-growth and score-first health should stay out.

## Findings
### Finding 1: Static markdown reference integrity is the only clear adopt-now slice
- **Source**: [README.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/README.md#L72), [claims.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/claims.ts#L48), [drift/index.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/index.ts#L17), [path.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/path.ts#L8), [edges.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/edges.ts#L5), [index-sync.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/index-sync.ts#L6)
- **What it does**: Mex extracts typed markdown claims from inline code, code blocks, and dependency headings, then runs zero-token checks for missing paths, dead frontmatter edges, and `patterns/INDEX.md` drift. It already distinguishes real missing references from pattern/template placeholders by downgrading some path misses to warnings.
- **Why it matters for us**: This cleanly maps to our real gap. Spec Kit already has semantic retrieval, trigger recall, causal links, and health tooling, but it does not statically verify that markdown references still point to real files or that pattern indexes stay in sync.
- **Recommendation**: adopt now
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 2: Dual freshness signals are useful, but only as supplemental trust metadata
- **Source**: [staleness.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/staleness.ts#L4), [git.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/git.ts#L12), [shared-payload.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/lib/context/shared-payload.ts#L22), [session-bootstrap.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/session-bootstrap.ts#L219), [memory-triggers.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-triggers.ts#L329)
- **What it does**: Mex emits separate stale-file issues from both elapsed days (`30`/`90`) and commits since last change (`50`/`200`). If git history cannot answer, `git.ts` returns `null`, so the checker silently emits nothing.
- **Why it matters for us**: The days-plus-commits idea is strong, but silent `null` is too weak for Spec Kit. Our current surfaces already distinguish `exact`, `estimated`, `defaulted`, `unknown`, and degraded matching; freshness should plug into that trust model instead of pretending “no signal” means “healthy.”
- **Recommendation**: prototype later
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 3: Mex’s repair brief flow is worth building as a provider-neutral Spec Kit feature
- **Source**: [sync/index.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/sync/index.ts#L29), [brief-builder.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/sync/brief-builder.ts#L7)
- **What it does**: `mex sync` groups issues by file, builds one combined brief, includes the current markdown, issue list, nearby filesystem listings for missing paths, and `HEAD~5..HEAD` diffs for referenced paths, then runs an interactive repair loop and re-checks drift after each cycle.
- **Why it matters for us**: This is the best “AI-assisted” idea in Mex. It converts static failures into bounded, auditable repair work instead of re-running broad doc rewrites. That fits Spec Kit’s packet-local remediation style very well.
- **Recommendation**: NEW FEATURE
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 4: Command, dependency, cross-file, and script-coverage audits are good ideas, but Mex’s implementation is too Node-centric for direct adoption
- **Source**: [command.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/command.ts#L5), [dependency.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/dependency.ts#L38), [cross-file.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/cross-file.ts#L3), [script-coverage.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/drift/checkers/script-coverage.ts#L26), [manifest.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/scanner/manifest.ts#L48)
- **What it does**: Mex validates npm/bun/yarn/pnpm scripts and Make targets, checks package dependencies and versions against `package.json`, flags version contradictions across docs, and warns if package scripts never appear in scaffold text. Non-Node manifests are mostly stubbed.
- **Why it matters for us**: We do need broader wrapper/config/doc parity checks, but our truth surfaces span shell commands, MCP tools, Python, TS, generated docs, and spec packets. Mex’s current inventory model is too narrow to trust in our repo.
- **Recommendation**: NEW FEATURE
- **Impact**: medium

### Finding 5: Scanner-first setup briefs are useful for bootstrapping, but not for durable truth maintenance
- **Source**: [README.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/README.md#L50), [SETUP.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/SETUP.md#L13), [scanner/index.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/scanner/index.ts#L20), [manifest.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/external/src/scanner/manifest.ts#L12)
- **What it does**: `mex init` builds a structured brief from manifest, entry points, folder tree, tooling, and README, then tells the AI to populate scaffold files from that brief rather than from raw browsing.
- **Why it matters for us**: This is good for first-pass scaffold seeding or packet bootstrap because it reduces exploratory noise. It is not good enough to become an authority layer for Spec Kit memory or documentation parity, especially with shallow non-Node support and no richer trust contract.
- **Recommendation**: prototype later
- **Impact**: low

    return null;

    return null;

/* ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   7. COMPACTION HOOK (TM-05)
──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────── */

/**
 * autoSurfaceAtCompaction
 *
 * Fires at session compaction lifecycle points. Surfaces memories relevant
 * to the ongoing session context so that critical knowledge is preserved
 * across the compaction boundary.
 *
 * Skipped when:
 *   - sessionContext is empty or too short to extract signal
 *   - enableCompactionHook is false in the integration config
 *
 * Token budget: COMPACTION_TOKEN_BUDGET (4000 max)
 *
 * @param sessionContext - A textual summary of the current session state
 * @param options        - Optional integration-layer config flags
 * @returns AutoSurfaceResult or null if nothing to surface / hook disabled
 */
async function autoSurfaceAtCompaction(
  sessionContext: string,
  options?: { enableCompactionHook?: boolean }
): Promise<AutoSurfaceResult | null> {
  // Allow integration layer to disable this hook via config flag
  if (options && options.enableCompactionHook === false) {
    return null;
  }

  // Require a meaningful context string (at least 3 characters)
  if (!sessionContext || typeof sessionContext !== 'string' || sessionContext.trim().length < 3) {
    return null;
  }

  // Delegate to the core surface function; token budget is explicitly
  // Enforced at the hook output boundary via estimateTokenCount().
  return autoSurfaceMemories(sessionContext.trim(), COMPACTION_TOKEN_BUDGET, 'compaction');
}

/* ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   8. EXPORTS
──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────── */

export {
  // Constants
  MEMORY_AWARE_TOOLS,
  CONSTITUTIONAL_CACHE_TTL,
  TOOL_DISPATCH_TOKEN_BUDGET,
  COMPACTION_TOKEN_BUDGET,

  // Functions
  extractContextHint,
  getConstitutionalMemories,
  clearConstitutionalCache,
  autoSurfaceMemories,
  primeSessionIfNeeded,
  resetSessionPrimed,
  autoSurfaceAtToolDispatch,
  autoSurfaceAtCompaction,

  // T018: Session tracking for session_health tool
  recordToolCall,
  getSessionTimestamps,
  getLastActiveSessionId,
  isSessionPrimed,
  markSessionPrimed,
  getCodeGraphStatusSnapshot,
};

export type { PrimePackage, AutoSurfaceResult };

# Iteration 021: CROSS-SYSTEM PATTERNS

## Focus
CROSS-SYSTEM PATTERNS: compare Mex against Engram, Modus Memory, OpenCode Mnemosyne, and MemPalace, then separate the patterns that recur across all five systems from the ones that are uniquely valuable in Mex.

## Findings
### Finding 1: The shared win is a thin agent-facing operating layer over a stronger core
- **Source**: [iteration-005.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/001-engram-main/research/iterations/iteration-005.md), [iteration-016.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/003-modus-memory-main/research/iterations/iteration-016.md), [research.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/research/research.md), [iteration-018.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/005-mempalace/research/iterations/iteration-018.md), [session-bootstrap.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/session-bootstrap.ts)
- **What it does**: Engram uses explicit lifecycle verbs, Mnemosyne uses thin recall/store wrappers plus compaction guidance, MemPalace uses status/protocol plus hooks, Modus uses a compact doctor surface, and Mex uses scaffold/drift/sync commands. Across all five, the usable part is the small operational surface, not the storage engine itself.
- **Why it matters**: Public already has the stronger substrate in `session_bootstrap`, `memory_context`, trigger recall, and governed saves. The missing piece is a thinner, easier-to-teach facade over those internals.
- **Recommendation**: NEW FEATURE
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 2: Systems stay useful only when preservation and recovery checkpoints are explicit
- **Source**: [iteration-005.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/001-engram-main/research/iterations/iteration-005.md), [research.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/research/research.md), [iteration-018.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/005-mempalace/research/iterations/iteration-018.md), [spec-kit-compact-code-graph.js](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/plugins/spec-kit-compact-code-graph.js), [memory-surface.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/hooks/memory-surface.ts)
- **What it does**: Engram has explicit session packaging, Mnemosyne injects compaction-time memory actions, MemPalace blocks on save/pre-compact hooks, and Mex runs explicit sync/drift cycles instead of assuming docs stay correct on their own.
- **Why it matters**: The cross-system lesson is that “memory exists” is not enough; agents need forced recovery or preservation moments. Public already has compaction and bootstrap infrastructure, so this is mostly about making the memory checkpoint more explicit.
- **Recommendation**: adopt now
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 3: Trust-first diagnostics converge; silent fallback and score-first health do not
- **Source**: [iteration-016.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/003-modus-memory-main/research/iterations/iteration-016.md), [iteration-020.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/research/iterations/iteration-020.md), [research.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/research/research.md), [session-bootstrap.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/session-bootstrap.ts)
- **What it does**: Modus shows the danger of “degraded” paths that still break, Mex shows why a single drift score hides real severity, Mnemosyne highlights the need for real readiness/warmup surfaces, and Public already carries explicit certainty states like `exact`, `estimated`, `defaulted`, and `unknown`.
- **Why it matters**: The common pattern is not “show one health number.” It is “surface whether the answer is trustworthy, partial, or unavailable.” That aligns directly with Public’s existing trust model.
- **Recommendation**: adopt now
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 4: Scope and mutation authority must stay governed even when ergonomics improve
- **Source**: [iteration-005.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/001-engram-main/research/iterations/iteration-005.md), [research.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/research/research.md), [iteration-018.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/005-mempalace/research/iterations/iteration-018.md), [memory-context.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-context.ts), [memory-triggers.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-triggers.ts)
- **What it does**: Engram’s lifecycle and topic boundaries, Mnemosyne’s project/global split, MemPalace’s separate fact plane, and Modus’s failure modes all reinforce the same rule: convenience surfaces are acceptable only when they compile down to a trusted scope and audited mutation model.
- **Why it matters**: Public is already closer to the right default here than any external system in this set. The safe direction is ergonomic aliases over existing authority, not cheaper write paths or weaker identity rules.
- **Recommendation**: reject
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 5: Mex is uniquely valuable because it checks documentation truth against the filesystem, not because it stores memory better
- **Source**: [iteration-020.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/research/iterations/iteration-020.md)
- **What it does**: Mex’s standout mechanism is typed markdown claim extraction plus zero-token path, edge, index, and freshness checking. None of the other four phases contributed a comparably strong docs-to-code integrity layer.
- **Why it matters**: This is the one area where Mex adds genuinely new capability to Public rather than overlapping with retrieval, session recovery, or local-memory ergonomics we already have.
- **Recommendation**: adopt now
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 6: Mex’s repair-brief loop is also unique, but its auto-growth and score-centric habits are the wrong transplant
- **Source**: [iteration-020.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/research/iterations/iteration-020.md)
- **What it does**: `mex sync` turns failed drift checks into bounded repair briefs with local file context and recent diffs, while `pattern add`, scaffold GROW defaults, and the single drift score push partially trusted content and compressed health reporting too early.
- **Why it matters**: The repair loop fits Public’s packet-local remediation style very well. The auto-growth and score-first pieces cut directly against Public’s trust-sensitive memory model.
- **Recommendation**: NEW FEATURE
- **Impact**: medium

## Assessment
- New information ratio: 0.43

## Recommended Next Focus
Spec one Public-native “memory integrity and continuity facade” packet with four bounded slices: 1. packet-local markdown path/edge/index drift checks, 2. compaction-time memory action card, 3. thin lifecycle/doctor aliases over existing MCP authority, 4. provider-neutral repair briefs generated from failed integrity checks.

# Iteration 021: CROSS-SYSTEM PATTERNS

## Focus
CROSS-SYSTEM PATTERNS: compare Mex against Engram, Modus Memory, OpenCode Mnemosyne, and MemPalace, then separate the patterns that recur across all five systems from the ones that are uniquely valuable in Mex.

## Findings
### Finding 1: The shared win is a thin agent-facing operating layer over a stronger core
- **Source**: [iteration-005.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/001-engram-main/research/iterations/iteration-005.md), [iteration-016.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/003-modus-memory-main/research/iterations/iteration-016.md), [research.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/research/research.md), [iteration-018.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/005-mempalace/research/iterations/iteration-018.md), [session-bootstrap.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/session-bootstrap.ts)
- **What it does**: Engram uses explicit lifecycle verbs, Mnemosyne uses thin recall/store wrappers plus compaction guidance, MemPalace uses status/protocol plus hooks, Modus uses a compact doctor surface, and Mex uses scaffold/drift/sync commands. Across all five, the usable part is the small operational surface, not the storage engine itself.
- **Why it matters**: Public already has the stronger substrate in `session_bootstrap`, `memory_context`, trigger recall, and governed saves. The missing piece is a thinner, easier-to-teach facade over those internals.
- **Recommendation**: NEW FEATURE
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 2: Systems stay useful only when preservation and recovery checkpoints are explicit
- **Source**: [iteration-005.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/001-engram-main/research/iterations/iteration-005.md), [research.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/research/research.md), [iteration-018.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/005-mempalace/research/iterations/iteration-018.md), [spec-kit-compact-code-graph.js](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/plugins/spec-kit-compact-code-graph.js), [memory-surface.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/hooks/memory-surface.ts)
- **What it does**: Engram has explicit session packaging, Mnemosyne injects compaction-time memory actions, MemPalace blocks on save/pre-compact hooks, and Mex runs explicit sync/drift cycles instead of assuming docs stay correct on their own.
- **Why it matters**: The cross-system lesson is that “memory exists” is not enough; agents need forced recovery or preservation moments. Public already has compaction and bootstrap infrastructure, so this is mostly about making the memory checkpoint more explicit.
- **Recommendation**: adopt now
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 3: Trust-first diagnostics converge; silent fallback and score-first health do not
- **Source**: [iteration-016.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/003-modus-memory-main/research/iterations/iteration-016.md), [iteration-020.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/research/iterations/iteration-020.md), [research.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/research/research.md), [session-bootstrap.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/session-bootstrap.ts)
- **What it does**: Modus shows the danger of “degraded” paths that still break, Mex shows why a single drift score hides real severity, Mnemosyne highlights the need for real readiness/warmup surfaces, and Public already carries explicit certainty states like `exact`, `estimated`, `defaulted`, and `unknown`.
- **Why it matters**: The common pattern is not “show one health number.” It is “surface whether the answer is trustworthy, partial, or unavailable.” That aligns directly with Public’s existing trust model.
- **Recommendation**: adopt now
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 4: Scope and mutation authority must stay governed even when ergonomics improve
- **Source**: [iteration-005.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/001-engram-main/research/iterations/iteration-005.md), [research.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/004-opencode-mnemosyne-main/research/research.md), [iteration-018.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/005-mempalace/research/iterations/iteration-018.md), [memory-context.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-context.ts), [memory-triggers.ts](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skill/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-triggers.ts)
- **What it does**: Engram’s lifecycle and topic boundaries, Mnemosyne’s project/global split, MemPalace’s separate fact plane, and Modus’s failure modes all reinforce the same rule: convenience surfaces are acceptable only when they compile down to a trusted scope and audited mutation model.
- **Why it matters**: Public is already closer to the right default here than any external system in this set. The safe direction is ergonomic aliases over existing authority, not cheaper write paths or weaker identity rules.
- **Recommendation**: reject
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 5: Mex is uniquely valuable because it checks documentation truth against the filesystem, not because it stores memory better
- **Source**: [iteration-020.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/research/iterations/iteration-020.md)
- **What it does**: Mex’s standout mechanism is typed markdown claim extraction plus zero-token path, edge, index, and freshness checking. None of the other four phases contributed a comparably strong docs-to-code integrity layer.
- **Why it matters**: This is the one area where Mex adds genuinely new capability to Public rather than overlapping with retrieval, session recovery, or local-memory ergonomics we already have.
- **Recommendation**: adopt now
- **Impact**: high

### Finding 6: Mex’s repair-brief loop is also unique, but its auto-growth and score-centric habits are the wrong transplant
- **Source**: [iteration-020.md](/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/specs/system-spec-kit/999-hybrid-rag-fusion-upgrade/001-research-hybrid-rag-fusion-systems/002-mex-main/research/iterations/iteration-020.md)
- **What it does**: `mex sync` turns failed drift checks into bounded repair briefs with local file context and recent diffs, while `pattern add`, scaffold GROW defaults, and the single drift score push partially trusted content and compressed health reporting too early.
- **Why it matters**: The repair loop fits Public’s packet-local remediation style very well. The auto-growth and score-first pieces cut directly against Public’s trust-sensitive memory model.
- **Recommendation**: NEW FEATURE
- **Impact**: medium

## Assessment
- New information ratio: 0.43

## Recommended Next Focus
Spec one Public-native “memory integrity and continuity facade” packet with four bounded slices: 1. packet-local markdown path/edge/index drift checks, 2. compaction-time memory action card, 3. thin lifecycle/doctor aliases over existing MCP authority, 4. provider-neutral repair briefs generated from failed integrity checks.
